<div id="Arab_revolt_inMandatory_Palestine" style="font-size:114%"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><strong class="selflink">Arab revolt in<br />
Mandatory Palestine</strong></span></div>
</th>

<p>The <b>1936–39 Arab revolt in Palestine</b> was a nationalist uprising by Palestinian Arabs in <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a> against the British administration of the Palestine Mandate, demanding Arab independence and the end of Jewish immigration as the League of Nations had authorized in 1922. The dissent was directly influenced by the Qassamite rebellion, following the killing of Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Izz_ad-Din_al-Qassam" title="Izz ad-Din al-Qassam">Izz ad-Din al-Qassam</a> in 1935, as well as the declaration by Hajj <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Amin_al-Husayni" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammad Amin al-Husayni">Mohammad Amin al-Husayni</a> of 16 May 1930 as 'Palestine Day' and calling for a <a href="/wiki/Arab_general_strike_(Mandatory_Palestine)" title="Arab general strike (Mandatory Palestine)">General Strike</a>. The revolt was branded by many in the Jewish <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">Yishuv</a> as "immoral and terroristic", often comparing it to fascism and nazism.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._136_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._136-10">[10]</a></sup> Ben Gurion however described Arab causes as fear of growing Jewish economic power, opposition to mass <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">Jewish immigration</a> and fear of the English identification with Zionism.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._136_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._136-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_general_strike_(Mandatory_Palestine)" title="Arab general strike (Mandatory Palestine)">general strike</a> lasted from April to October 1936, initiating the violent revolt. The revolt consisted of two distinct phases.<sup id="cite_ref-norris2008_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris2008-11">[11]</a></sup> The first phase was directed primarily by the urban and elitist <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">Higher Arab Committee</a> (HAC) and was focused mainly on strikes and other forms of political protest.<sup id="cite_ref-norris2008_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris2008-11">[11]</a></sup> By October 1936, this phase had been defeated by the British <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioners_for_Palestine_and_Transjordan" title="High Commissioners for Palestine and Transjordan">civil administration</a> using a combination of <a href="/wiki/Concession_(politics)" title="Concession (politics)">political concessions</a>, international diplomacy (involving the rulers of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iraq" title="Kingdom of Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutawakkilite_Kingdom_of_Yemen" title="Mutawakkilite Kingdom of Yemen">Yemen</a><sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup>) and the threat of <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-norris2008_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris2008-11">[11]</a></sup> The second phase, which began late in 1937, was a violent and peasant-led resistance movement that increasingly targeted British forces.<sup id="cite_ref-norris2008_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris2008-11">[11]</a></sup> During this phase, the rebellion was brutally suppressed by the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Police_Force" title="Palestine Police Force">Palestine Police Force</a> using repressive measures that were intended to intimidate the Arab population and undermine popular support for the revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-norris2008_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris2008-11">[11]</a></sup> During this phase, a more dominant role on the Arab side was taken by the <a href="/wiki/Nashashibi_clan" title="Nashashibi clan">Nashashibi clan</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/National_Defense_Party_(Mandatory_Palestine)" title="National Defense Party (Mandatory Palestine)">NDP party</a> quickly withdrew from the rebel <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">Arab Higher Committee</a>, led by the radical <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Arab_Party" title="Palestine Arab Party">faction</a> of Amin al-Husseini, and instead sided with the British – dispatching "Fasail al-Salam" (the "Peace Bands") in coordination with the British Army against nationalist and Jihadist Arab "Fasail" units (literally "bands").</p>
<p>According to official British figures covering the whole revolt, the army and police killed more than 2,000 Arabs in combat, 108 were <a href="/wiki/Hanging" title="Hanging">hanged</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-levenberg_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levenberg-8">[8]</a></sup> and 961 died because of what they described as "gang and terrorist activities".<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup> In an analysis of the British statistics, <a href="/wiki/Walid_Khalidi" title="Walid Khalidi">Walid Khalidi</a> estimates 19,792 casualties for the Arabs, with 5,032 dead: 3,832 killed by the British and 1,200 dead because of "terrorism", and 14,760 wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup> Over ten percent of the adult male <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Arab">Palestinian Arab</a> population between 20 and 60 was killed, wounded, imprisoned or exiled.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Estimates of the number of <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Jews" title="Palestinian Jews">Palestinian Jews</a> killed range from 91<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> to several hundred.<sup id="cite_ref-morris160_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morris160-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Arab revolt in Mandatory Palestine was unsuccessful, and its consequences affected the outcome of the <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestine_war" title="1948 Palestine war">1948 Palestine war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._159_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1999.2C_p._159-15">[15]</a></sup> It caused the British Mandate to give crucial support to pre-state Zionist militias like the <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">Haganah</a>, whereas on the Palestinian Arab side, the revolt forced the flight into exile of the main Palestinian Arab leader of the period, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Mufti_of_Jerusalem" title="Grand Mufti of Jerusalem">Grand Mufti of Jerusalem</a> – <a href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" class="mw-redirect" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">Haj Amin al-Husseini</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disputed_statement" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Disputed statement"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2015)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine#Dubious" title="Talk:1936–39 Arab revolt in Palestine">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cement_Incident" title="Cement Incident">Cement Incident</a> and <a href="/wiki/Izz_ad-Din_al-Qassam" title="Izz ad-Din al-Qassam">Izz ad-Din al-Qassam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="913" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_12857_Events_in_Israel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Funeral of Jews from <a href="/wiki/Givat_Ada" class="mw-redirect" title="Givat Ada">Givat Ada</a> that were killed in 1936.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1930 Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Izz_ad-Din_al-Qassam" title="Izz ad-Din al-Qassam">Izz ad-Din al-Qassam</a> organized and established the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hand_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Hand (Palestine)">Black Hand</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anti-Zionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Zionist">anti-Zionist</a> and anti-British militant organization. He recruited and arranged military training for peasants and by 1935 he had enlisted between 200 and 800 men. They were engaged in a campaign of vandalizing trees planted by farmers and British-constructed rail lines.<sup id="cite_ref-segev_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-segev-16">[16]</a></sup> In November 1935, two of his men engaged in a firefight with the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestine Police">Palestine Police</a> patrol hunting fruit thieves and a policeman was killed. Following the incident, the police launched a manhunt and surrounded al-Qassam in a cave near <a href="/wiki/Ya%27bad" title="Ya'bad">Ya'bad</a>. In the ensuing battle, al-Qassam was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-segev_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-segev-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The death of al-Qassam generated widespread outrage among Palestinian Arabs. Huge crowds accompanied Qassam's body to his grave in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dissent in Palestine was influenced also by the discovery in October 1935 at the port of <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">Jaffa</a> of a large <a href="/wiki/Cement_Incident" title="Cement Incident">arms shipment</a> destined for the <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">Haganah</a>, sparking Arab fears of a Jewish military takeover of Palestine,<sup id="cite_ref-matthews_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-matthews-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kramer263_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer263-19">[19]</a></sup> Jewish immigration also peaked in 1935, just months before Palestinian Arabs began a full-scale, nationwide revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In the four years between 1933 and 1936 more than 164,000 Jewish immigrants arrived in Palestine, and between 1931 and 1936 the Jewish population more than doubled from 175,000 to 370,000 people, increasing the Jewish population share from 17% to 27%, and bringing about a significant deterioration in relations between Palestinian Arabs and Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus,_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg/220px-Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg/330px-Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg/440px-Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus%2C_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="616" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Remains_of_a_burnt_Jewish_passenger_bus,_Result_of_terrorist_acts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Result of terrorist acts and government measures. Remains of a burnt Jewish passenger bus at Balad Esh-Sheikh outside Haifa. Picture taken between 1934 and 1938.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The uprising began with the <a href="/wiki/1936_Anabta_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="1936 Anabta shooting">1936 Anabta shooting</a>, a 15 April 1936 roadblock that stopped a convoy of trucks on the <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">Nablus</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tulkarm" title="Tulkarm">Tulkarm</a> road during which the (probably Qassamite)<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> assailants shot two Jewish drivers, Israel Khazan, who was killed instantly, and Zvi Dannenberg, who died five days later.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The next day members of the militant Jewish faction, the <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">Irgun</a>, shot and killed two Arab workers sleeping in a hut near <a href="/wiki/Petah_Tikva" title="Petah Tikva">Petah Tikva</a> in a revenge attack.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gilbert80_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gilbert80-26">[26]</a></sup> Then the funeral for Khazan in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> on 17 April attracted a huge crowd, and some Jews beat up Arab bystanders and destroyed property.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> This was followed by <a href="/wiki/The_Bloody_Day_in_Jaffa" title="The Bloody Day in Jaffa">the Bloody Day in Jaffa</a>, in which an Arab mob rampaged through a residential area killing Jews and destroying property.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> An Arab general strike and revolt ensued that lasted until October 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the summer of that year, thousands of Jewish-farmed acres and orchards were destroyed, Jewish civilians were attacked and murdered, and some Jewish communities, such as those in <a href="/wiki/Beisan" class="mw-redirect" title="Beisan">Beisan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, fled to safer areas.<sup id="cite_ref-gilbert80_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gilbert80-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_background">Economic background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Economic background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Palestinian_Products" title="Association for Palestinian Products">Association for Palestinian Products</a></div>
<p>Economic factors played a major role in the outbreak of the Arab revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> Palestine's <a href="/wiki/Fellahin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellahin">fellahin</a>, the country's peasant farmers, comprised over two-thirds of the indigenous Arab population and from the 1920s onwards they were pushed off the land in increasingly large numbers into urban environments where they often encountered only poverty and social marginalisation.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> Many were crowded into <a href="/wiki/Shanty_town" title="Shanty town">shanty towns</a> in Jaffa and Haifa where they found succor and encouragement in the teachings of the charismatic preacher Izz ad-Din al-Qassam who worked among the poor in Haifa.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The revolt was thus a popular uprising that produced its own leaders and developed into a national revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>World War I left Palestine, especially the countryside, deeply impoverished.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> and then the Mandate authorities levied high taxes on farming and agricultural produce and during the 1920s and 1930s this together with a fall in prices, cheap imports, natural disasters and paltry harvests all contributed to the increasing indebtedness of the fellahin.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The rents paid by tenant fellah increased sharply, owing to increased population density, and transfer of land from Arabs to the Jewish settlement agencies, such as the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Fund" title="Jewish National Fund">Jewish National Fund</a>, increased the number of fellahin evicted while also removing the land as a future source of livelihood.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> By 1931 the 106,400 <a href="/wiki/Dunam" title="Dunam">dunums</a> of low-lying Category A farming land in Arab possession supported a farming population of 590,000 whereas the 102,000 dunums of such land in Jewish possession supported a farming population of only 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The problem of 'landless' Arabs grew particularly grave after 1931, causing <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grenfell_Wauchope" title="Arthur Grenfell Wauchope">High Commissioner Wauchope</a> to warn that this 'social peril&#160;... would serve as a focus of discontent and might even result in serious disorders.'<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the Mandatory government introduced measures to limit the transfer of land from Arabs to Jews these were easily circumvented by willing buyers and sellers.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The failure of the authorities to invest in economic growth and healthcare and the Zionist policy of ensuring that their investments were directed only to facilitate expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">Yishuv</a> further compounded matters.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> The government did, however, set the minimum wage for Arab workers below that for Jewish workers, which meant that those making capital investments in the Yishuv's economic infrastructure, such as Haifa's electricity plant, the Shemen oil and soap factory, the Grands Moulins flour mills and the Nesher cement factory, could take advantage of cheap Arab labour pouring in from the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> After 1935 the slump in the construction boom and further concentration by the Yishuv on an exclusivist Hebrew labour programme removed most of the sources of employment for rural migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup> By 1935 only 12,000 Arabs (5% of the workforce) worked in the Jewish sector, half of these in agriculture, whereas 32,000 worked for the Mandate authorities and 211,000 were either self-employed or worked for Arab employers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ongoing disruption of agrarian life in Palestine, which had been continuing since Ottoman times, thus created a large population of landless peasant farmers who subsequently became mobile wage workers who were increasingly marginalised and impoverished; these became willing participants in nationalist rebellion.<sup id="cite_ref-yazbak_29-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yazbak-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_socio-cultural_background">Political and socio-cultural background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political and socio-cultural background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarab_Abd_al-Hadi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Tarab_Abd_al-Hadi.jpg/220px-Tarab_Abd_al-Hadi.jpg" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/48/Tarab_Abd_al-Hadi.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="415" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarab_Abd_al-Hadi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Feminist activist <a href="/wiki/Tarab_Abdul_Hadi" title="Tarab Abdul Hadi">Tarab Abdul Hadi</a>, organiser of the Palestinian Arab Women's Association.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Initially, the conflict with Zionism helped to make Palestinian Arab society more conservative in cultural, social, religious and political affairs because people were highly motivated to preserve their distinct heritage and identity against the dual impact of British colonialism and Jewish innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer239_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer239-31">[31]</a></sup> Traditionally, the Arabs had an elite, but not a real leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer239_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer239-31">[31]</a></sup> Both of these things changed over the course of the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer239_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer239-31">[31]</a></sup> During this period new political organizations and new types of activist began to appear, marking the involvement of a far broader cross-section of the population; in particular, nationalism, which had been long-rooted in rural society began to take hold in urban society.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer254_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer254-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Youth organisations proliferated at this time; these included the <a href="/wiki/Young_Men%27s_Muslim_Association" title="Young Men's Muslim Association">Young Men's Muslim Association</a>, which from 1931 agitated for armed resistance against the Zionists, the <a href="/wiki/Youth_Congress_Party" title="Youth Congress Party">Youth Congress Party</a>, which expressed pan-Arab sentiments, and the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Scout_Association" title="Palestinian Scout Association">Palestinian Boy Scout Movement</a>, founded early in 1936, which became active in the general strike.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer254_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer254-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Women's organisations, which had been active in social matters, became politically involved from the end of the 1920s, with an Arab Women's Congress held in Jerusalem in 1929 attracting 200 participants, and an Arab Women's Association (later Arab Women's Union) being established at the same time, both organised by feminist <a href="/wiki/Tarab_Abdul_Hadi" title="Tarab Abdul Hadi">Tarab Abdul Hadi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer254_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer254-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PASSIApub_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PASSIApub-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the beginning of the 1930s new political parties began to appear, including the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence Party (Palestine)">Independence Party</a>, which called for an <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian Congress Party</a>-style boycott of the British,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> the pro-<a href="/wiki/Nashashibi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nashashibi">Nashashibi</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Defence_Party_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Defence Party (Palestine)">National Defence Party</a>, the pro-<a href="/wiki/Husayni" class="mw-redirect" title="Husayni">Husayni</a> <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Arab_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Arab Party">Palestinian Arab Party</a> the pro-Khalidi <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Reform Party (Palestine)">Arab-Palestinian Reform Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Bloc_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Bloc (Palestine)">National Bloc</a>, based mainly around Nablus.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer259_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer259-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>A few militant secret societies, which advocated armed struggle were formed; these included the Green Hand, which was active in the hills around <a href="/wiki/Safad" class="mw-redirect" title="Safad">Safad</a>, but eliminated by the British in 1931, the Organization for Holy Struggle, led by <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Qadir_al-Husayni" title="Abd al-Qadir al-Husayni">Abd al-Qadir al-Husayni</a> and active in the Hebron area, which was later to play an important role in the <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestine_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1948 Palestine War">1948 Palestine War</a>, and the Young Rebels or Avenging Youth, active in the <a href="/wiki/Tulkarm" title="Tulkarm">Tulkarm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qalqilyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Qalqilyah">Qalqilyah</a> area from 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer259_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer259-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Traditional feasts such as <a href="/wiki/Nebi_Musa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nebi Musa">Nebi Musa</a> began to acquire a political and nationalist dimension and new national memorial days were introduced or gained new significance; among them Balfour Day (2 November, marking the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1917" class="mw-redirect" title="Balfour Declaration of 1917">Balfour Declaration of 1917</a>), the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hattin" title="Battle of Hattin">Battle of Hattin</a> (4 July, marking <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Saladin</a>'s recapture of Jerusalem), and beginning in 1930 May 16 was celebrated as Palestine Day.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer259_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer259-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The expansion of education, the development of <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> and of transportation, communications, and especially of broadcasting and other media, all facilitated these changes.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_political_background">Regional political background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Regional political background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of political changes in neighbouring Arab countries illustrated to the Palestinian Arabs what could be achieved in a Western colony through political pressure and negotiating skill.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Syria a general strike took place from 20 January to 6 March 1936 spreading to all the major towns, and political demonstrations held throughout the country gave fresh momentum to the Syrian national movement. Although French reprisals were harsh the government agreed on 2 March to the formation of a Syrian delegation to travel to Paris to negotiate a <a href="/wiki/Franco-Syrian_Treaty_of_Independence_(1936)" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Syrian Treaty of Independence (1936)">Franco-Syrian Treaty of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> This demonstrated that determined economic and political pressure could challenge a fragile imperial administration.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> on 2 March 1936 a series of formal negotiations between the United Kingdom and Egypt began leading to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Treaty_of_1936" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Egyptian Treaty of 1936">Anglo-Egyptian Treaty of 1936</a>, which granted independence to Egypt, but allowed the British to keep forces in the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal Zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Iraq a general strike in July 1931, accompanied by organised demonstrations in the streets, led to independence for the former British mandate territory under prime minister <a href="/wiki/Nuri_as-Said" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuri as-Said">Nuri as-Said</a>, and full membership of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> in October 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_General_Strike_and_armed_insurrection">Arab General Strike and armed insurrection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Arab General Strike and armed insurrection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_general_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian general strike">Palestinian general strike</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/1936_Syrian_general_strike" title="1936 Syrian general strike">1936 Syrian general strike</a> and <a href="/wiki/1936_Anabta_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="1936 Anabta shooting">1936 Anabta shooting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg/220px-Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg/330px-Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg/440px-Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="3371" data-file-height="2445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wauchope_1936_and_Allenby_1917_Cartoon_in_Falastin_June_1936.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
June 1936 cartoon in <i><a href="/wiki/Falastin_(newspaper)" title="Falastin (newspaper)">Falastin</a></i> contrasting the actions of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grenfell_Wauchope" title="Arthur Grenfell Wauchope">Wauchope</a> in 1936 against those of <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Allenby,_1st_Viscount_Allenby" title="Edmund Allenby, 1st Viscount Allenby">Allenby</a> in 1917</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khalil_Sakakini.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/92/Khalil_Sakakini.jpg" width="200" height="264" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khalil_Sakakini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Khalil_al-Sakakini" title="Khalil al-Sakakini">Khalil al-Sakakini</a> called the revolt a "life-and-death struggle."<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The strike began on 19 April in Nablus, where an Arab National Committee was formed,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-peel96_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel96-45">[45]</a></sup> and by the end of the month National Committees had been formed in all of the towns and some of the larger villages.<sup id="cite_ref-peel96_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel96-45">[45]</a></sup> On 21 April the leaders of the five main parties accepted the decision at Nablus and called for a general strike of all Arabs engaged in labour, transport and shopkeeping for the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-peel96_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel96-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the strike was initially organised by workers and local committees, under pressure from below, political leaders became involved to help with co-ordination.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> This led to the formation on 25 April 1936 of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">Arab Higher Committee</a> (AHC).<sup id="cite_ref-peel96_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel96-45">[45]</a></sup> The Committee resolved "to continue the general strike until the British Government changes its present policy in a fundamental manner"; the demands were threefold: (1) the prohibition of Jewish immigration; (2) the prohibition of the transfer of Arab land to Jews; (3) the establishment of a National Government responsible to a representative council.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_BG.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/David_BG.jpg/220px-David_BG.jpg" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/David_BG.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="292" data-file-height="436" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_BG.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">David Ben-Gurion</a> told mourners at a funeral held on 20 April 1936 for nine victims of rioting in <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">Jaffa</a> the previous day that Jews would only be safe "in communities which are 100% Jewish and built on Jewish land."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>About one month after the general strike started, the leadership group declared a general non-payment of taxes in explicit opposition to Jewish immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the countryside, armed insurrection started sporadically, becoming more organised with time.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> One particular target of the rebels was the <a href="/wiki/Mosul%E2%80%93Haifa_oil_pipeline" title="Mosul–Haifa oil pipeline">Mosul–Haifa oil pipeline</a> of the Iraq Petroleum Company constructed only a few years earlier to Haifa from a point on the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">Jordan River</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tiberias" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Tiberias">Lake Tiberias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> This was repeatedly bombed at various points along its length. Other attacks were on railways (including trains) and on civilian targets such as Jewish settlements, secluded Jewish neighbourhoods in the mixed cities, and Jews, both individually and in groups.<sup id="cite_ref-peel100_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel100-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The measures taken against the strike were harsh at the beginning and grew harsher as it went along involving house searches without warrants, night raids, preventive detention, caning, flogging, deportation, confiscation of property, and torture.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> As early as May 1936 the British formed armed Jewish units equipped with armoured vehicles to serve as auxiliary police.<sup id="cite_ref-Kr.C3.A4mer.2C_2008.2C_p._291_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kr.C3.A4mer.2C_2008.2C_p._291-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg/220px-Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg" width="220" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg/330px-Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg/440px-Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="621" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arab_strike_1936._Car_with_brooms_to_sweep_away_tacks_thrown_by_strikers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arab strike 1936. Car with brooms to sweep away tacks thrown by strikers.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The British government in Palestine was convinced that the strike had the full support of the Palestinian Arabs and they could see "no weakening in the will and spirit of the Arab people."<sup id="cite_ref-kay196_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kay196-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_Vice-Marshall" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Vice-Marshall">Air Vice-Marshall</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Peirse" title="Richard Peirse">Richard Peirse</a>, commander of British forces in Palestine and Transjordan from 1933 to 1936, reported that because the rebel armed bands were supported by villagers,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>It was quickly evident that the only way to regain the initiative from the rebels was by initiating measures against the villagers from which the rebels and saboteurs came&#160;... I therefore initiated, in co-operation with the Inspector-General of Police R. G. B. Spicer, village searches. Ostensibly, these searches were undertaken to find arms and wanted persons, actually the measures adopted by the Police on the lines of similar Turkish methods, were punitive and effective.<sup id="cite_ref-kay196_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kay196-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In reality the measures created a sense of solidarity between the villagers and the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-kay196_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kay196-56">[56]</a></sup> The pro-Government Mayor of Nablus complained to the High Commissioner that, "During the last searches effected in villages properties were destroyed, jewels stolen, and the Holy <a href="/wiki/Qu%27ran" class="mw-redirect" title="Qu'ran">Qu'ran</a> torn, and this has increased the excitement of the fellahin."<sup id="cite_ref-kay196_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kay196-56">[56]</a></sup> However, Moshe Shertok of the Jewish Agency even suggested that all villages in the area of an incident should be punished.<sup id="cite_ref-Segev.2C_2000.2C_p._423_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Segev.2C_2000.2C_p._423-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 June, an attempt by rebels to derail a train bringing the 2nd Battalion <a href="/wiki/Bedfordshire_and_Hertfordshire_Regiment" title="Bedfordshire and Hertfordshire Regiment">Bedfordshire and Hertfordshire Regiment</a> from Egypt led to the railways being put under guard, placing a great strain on the security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-horne213_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horne213-58">[58]</a></sup> In response to this situation on 4 June the government rounded up a large number of Palestinian leaders and sent them to a detention camp at <a href="/wiki/Auja_al-Hafir" title="Auja al-Hafir">Auja al-Hafir</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">Negev</a> desert.<sup id="cite_ref-horne213_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horne213-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nur_Shams" title="Battle of Nur Shams">Battle of Nur Shams</a> on 21 June marked an escalation with the largest engagement of British troops against Arab militants so far in this Revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-HeaviestFighting_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HeaviestFighting-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>During July, Arab volunteers from Syria and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Fawzi_al-Qawukji" class="mw-redirect" title="Fawzi al-Qawukji">Fawzi al-Qawukji</a>, helped the rebels to divide their formations into four fronts, each led by a District Commander who had armed platoons of 150–200 fighters, each commanded by a platoon leader.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>A Statement of Policy issued by the Colonial Office in London on 7 September declared the situation a: "direct challenge to the authority of the British Government in Palestine" and announced the appointment of Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/John_Dill" title="John Dill">John Dill</a> as supreme military commander.<sup id="cite_ref-peel100_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel100-53">[53]</a></sup> By the end of September 20,000 British troops in Palestine were deployed to "round up Arab bands".<sup id="cite_ref-peel100_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel100-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 1936 the British involved their clients in Transjordan, Iraq, Saudi Arabia and Egypt in an attempt to pacify the Palestinian Arabs and on 9 October the rulers made an appeal for the strike to be ended.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer278_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer278-61">[61]</a></sup> A more pressing concern may have been the approaching citrus harvest and the soaring prices that were available because of the disruption caused to the Spanish citrus harvest by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kramer278_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kramer278-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peel_commission">Peel commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Peel commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The strike was called off on 11 October 1936<sup id="cite_ref-peel100_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peel100-53">[53]</a></sup> and the violence abated for about a year while the <a href="/wiki/Peel_Commission" title="Peel Commission">Peel Commission</a> deliberated. The Royal Commission was announced on 18 May 1936 and its members were appointed on 29 July, but the Commission did not arrive in Palestine until 11 November.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Commission, which concluded that 1,000 Arab rebels had been killed during the strike, later described the disturbances as "an open rebellion of the Palestinian Arabs, assisted by fellow-Arabs from other countries, against Mandatory rule" and noted two unprecedented features of the revolt: the support of all senior Arab officials in the political and technical departments in the Palestine administration (including all of the Arab judges) and the "interest and sympathy of the neighbouring Arab peoples", which had resulted in support for the rebellion in the form of volunteers from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg/220px-Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg/330px-Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg/440px-Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="647" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lord_Peel_arrives.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/William_Peel,_1st_Earl_Peel" title="William Peel, 1st Earl Peel">Lord Peel</a> arrives in Mandatory Palestine 11 November 1936. Privately, Peel believed that most Jews would remain in the Diaspora.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 1920s the first High Commissioner of Palestine, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Samuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbert Samuel">Herbert Samuel</a>, failed to create a unified political structure embracing both Palestinian Arabs and Palestinian Jews in constitutional government with joint political institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup> This failure facilitated internal institutional partition in which the Jewish Agency exercised a degree of autonomous control over the Jewish settlement and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Muslim_Council" title="Supreme Muslim Council">Supreme Muslim Council</a> performed a comparable role for Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup> Thus, well before Lord Peel arrived in Palestine on 11 November 1936, the groundwork for territorial partition as proposed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission" title="Royal Commission">Royal Commission</a> in its report on 7 July 1937 had already been done.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg/220px-PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg/330px-PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg/440px-PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="373" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_297_Kibutz_Gan-Shmuel_sk1-_38_%D7%92%D7%9F-%D7%A9%D7%9E%D7%95%D7%90%D7%9C_-_%D7%90%D7%A9_%D7%91%D7%A9%D7%93%D7%95%D7%AA_1936-9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fields on fire at the <a href="/wiki/Gan_Shmuel" title="Gan Shmuel">Gan-Shmuel</a> Kibbutz. Picture taken between 1936 and 1939.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Peel's main recommendation was for partition of Palestine into a small Jewish state (based on current Jewish land ownership population and incorporating the country's most productive agricultural land), a residual Mandatory area, and a larger Arab state linked to <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup> A second and more radical proposal was for transfer of 225,000 Palestinian Arabs from the Jewish state to the Arab state and Transjordan.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup> It is likely that Zionist leaders played a role in persuading Peel to accept the notion of transfer, which had been a strand of Zionist ideology from its inception.<sup id="cite_ref-morrispeel_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrispeel-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Arab Higher Committee rejected the recommendations immediately,<sup id="cite_ref-morrispeel_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrispeel-66">[66]</a></sup> as did the Jewish <a href="/wiki/Revisionist_Zionism" title="Revisionist Zionism">Revisionists</a>. Initially, the <a href="/wiki/Mizrachi_(religious_Zionism)" title="Mizrachi (religious Zionism)">religious Zionists</a>, some of the <a href="/wiki/General_Zionists" title="General Zionists">General Zionists</a>, and sections of the <a href="/wiki/Labor_Zionism" title="Labor Zionism">Labour Zionist</a> movement opposed the recommendations.<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup> Ben-Gurion was delighted by the Peel Commission's support for transfer, which he viewed as the foundation of "national consolidation in a free homeland."<sup id="cite_ref-morrispeel_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrispeel-66">[66]</a></sup> Subsequently, the 2 main Jewish leaders, <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">Chaim Weizmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">Ben Gurion</a> had convinced the <a href="/wiki/World_Zionist_Congress" title="World Zionist Congress">Zionist Congress</a> to approve equivocally the Peel recommendations as a basis for further negotiation,<sup id="cite_ref-wasserstein_65-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wasserstein-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Louis2006p391_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louis2006p391-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Morris2004p11_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris2004p11-68">[68]</a></sup> and to negotiate a modified Peel proposal with the British.<sup id="cite_ref-RaiderSarna2012_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaiderSarna2012-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British government initially accepted the Peel report in principle. However, with war clouds looming over Europe, they realized that to attempt to implement it against the will of the Palestinian Arab majority would rouse up the entire Arab world against Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-Wasserstein2012p339_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wasserstein2012p339-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Woodhead_Commission" title="Woodhead Commission">Woodhead Commission</a> considered three different plans, one of which was based on the Peel plan. Reporting in 1938, the Commission rejected the Peel plan primarily on the grounds that it could not be implemented without a massive forced transfer of Arabs (an option that the British government had already ruled out).<sup id="cite_ref-WoodheadReport1938_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WoodheadReport1938-71">[71]</a></sup> With dissent from some of its members, the Commission instead recommended a plan that would leave the Galilee under British mandate, but emphasised serious problems with it that included a lack of financial self-sufficiency of the proposed Arab State.<sup id="cite_ref-WoodheadReport1938_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WoodheadReport1938-71">[71]</a></sup> The British Government accompanied the publication of the Woodhead Report by a statement of policy rejecting partition as impracticable due to "political, administrative and financial difficulties".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resumed_Revolt_.28September_1937_.E2.80.93_August_1939.29">Resumed Revolt (September 1937 – August 1939)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Resumed Revolt (September 1937 – August 1939)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/1938_Tiberias_massacre" title="1938 Tiberias massacre">1938 Tiberias massacre</a></div>
<p>With the failure of the Peel Commission's proposals the revolt resumed during the autumn of 1937 marked by the assassination on 26 September of Acting District Commissioner of the Galilee <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Yelland_Andrews" title="Lewis Yelland Andrews">Lewis Andrews</a> by Arab gunmen in Nazareth.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen.2C_2009.2C_p._125_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen.2C_2009.2C_p._125-73">[73]</a></sup> On 30 September, regulations were issued allowing the Government to detain political deportees in any part of the British Empire, and authorizing the High Commissioner to outlaw associations whose objectives he regarded as contrary to public policy. <a href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" class="mw-redirect" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">Haj Amin al-Husseini</a> was removed from the leadership of the Supreme Moslem Council and the General Waqf Committee, the local National Committees and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">Arab Higher Committee</a> were disbanded; five Arab leaders were arrested and deported to the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>; and in fear of arrest Jamal el-Husseini fled to Syria and Haj Amin el-Husseini to Lebanon;<sup id="cite_ref-avalon_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avalon-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-horne222_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horne222-75">[75]</a></sup> all frontiers with Palestine were closed, telephone connections to neighbouring countries were withdrawn, press censorship was introduced and a special <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a> was opened near Acre.<sup id="cite_ref-horne222_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horne222-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1937, the <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">Irgun</a> formally rejected the policy of <a href="/wiki/Havlagah" title="Havlagah">Havlagah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sunday,_1937" title="Black Sunday, 1937">embarked on a series of indiscriminate attacks</a> against Arab civilians as a form of what the group called "active defense" against Arab attacks on Jewish civilians. The British authorities set up military courts, which were established for the trial of offenses connected with the carrying and discharge of firearms, sabotage and intimidation. Despite this, however, the Arab campaign of murder and sabotage continued and Arab gangs in the hills took on the appearance of organized guerrilla fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-avalon_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avalon-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Violence continued throughout 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-1">[1]</a></sup> In July 1938, when the Palestine Government seemed to have largely lost control of the situation, the garrison was strengthened from Egypt, and in September it was further reinforced from England. The police were placed under the operational control of the army commander, and military officials superseded the civil authorities in the enforcement of order. In October the Old City of Jerusalem, which had become a rebel stronghold, was reoccupied by the troops. By the end of the year a semblance of order had been restored in the towns, but terrorism continued in rural areas until the outbreak of the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-avalon_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avalon-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite cooperation of the Yishuv with the British to quell the revolt, some incidents towards the end of the conflict indicated a coming change in relations. On 12 June 1939, A British explosives expert was killed trying to defuse an Irgun bomb near a <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> post office. On 26 August, two British police officers, Inspector Ronald Barker and Inspector <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Cairns" title="Ralph Cairns">Ralph Cairns</a>, commander of the Jewish Department of the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department" title="Criminal Investigation Department">C.I.D.</a>, were killed by an Irgun mine in Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the final fifteen months of the revolt alone there were 936 murders and 351 attempted murders; 2,125 incidents of sniping; 472 bombs thrown and detonated; 364 cases of armed robbery; 1,453 cases of sabotage against government and commercial property; 323 people abducted; 72 cases of intimidation; 236 Jews killed by Arabs and 435 Arabs killed by Jews; 1,200 rebels killed by the police and military and 535 wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-horne_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horne-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Response">Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_the_Mandate_Government_and_the_British_Army">Role of the Mandate Government and the British Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1936%E2%80%9339_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Role of the Mandate Government and the British Army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Al-Bassa" title="Al-Bassa">al-Bassa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halhul" title="Halhul">Halhul</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palest_against_british.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Palest_against_british.gif/220px-Palest_against_british.gif" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Palest_against_british.gif/330px-Palest_against_british.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Palest_against_british.gif/440px-Palest_against_british.gif 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="401" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palest_against_british.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Arab revolt of 1936–39 in Palestine</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/220px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/330px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg/440px-Havlagah_bus_during_1936-1939_Arab_revolt-British_Mandate_of_Palestine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="890" data-file-height="487" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
